)@@G@@*[S@@@*SDFF*@A@@@@THE TAPE ANALYSIS PROCESSOR (RAT)   @]@@@@RIGHTM ON   QG
)@@G@@@]@@@@HYPHEN ON   @]@@@@1PURPOSE    @E@@@@ QUITE OFTEN A TAPE MAY MAGICAQH
)@@G@@LLY APPEAR FROM SOME UNKNOWN  @E@@@@ SITE, CONSISTING OF SOME UNKNOWN QUQI
)@@G@@ANTITY OF UNKNOWN DATA. @D@@@@ IT COULD BE ANY DENSITY OR PARITY. AND WHQJ
)@@G@@O KNOWS WHAT@E@@@@ CHARACTER CODE IT WAS WRITTEN IN. THIS PROCESSOR HAS QK
)@@G@@BEEN  @B@@@@ WRITTEN TO HELP ALLEVIATE THE MYSTERY.   @]@@@@SPACE 1     QL
)@@G@@@A@@@@ WHY RAT? BECAUSE IT 'READS A TAPE'.@#@@@@1PROCESSOR INPUT  @A@@@@QM
)@@G@@ THE INPUT TO THE PROGRAM IS A TAPE.@]@@@@SPACE 1     @A@@@@ THE PROCESSQN
)@@G@@OR IS CALLED BY ...     @]@@@@SPACE 1     @A@@@@     @RAT,<OPTIONS>   FIQO
)@@G@@LENAME.     @]@@@@SPACE 1     @E@@@@ THE ONLY OPTION CURRENTLY USED IS 'QP
)@@G@@N'. THIS INDICATES THAT @D@@@@ THE TAPE IS ALREADY IN THE CORRECT MODE FQQ
)@@G@@OR READING. @]@@@@SPACE 0     @F@@@@ THE FILENAME IS THE NAME OF THE PREQR
)@@G@@VIOUSLY ASSIGNED TAPE FILE.   @]@@@@SPACE 1     @E@@@@ IT IS THE RESPONSQS
)@@G@@IBILITY OF THE USER TO ASSIGN THE TAPE    @D@@@@ TO A DRIVE THAT WILL BEQT
)@@G@@ ABLE TO READ IT. BUT IN CASE @D@@@@ HE DOESN'T AND THE PROGRAM FAILS ALQU
)@@G@@L ATTEMPTS, A     @D@@@@ SUGGESTION WILL BE MADE ABOUT TRYING A DIFFERENQV
)@@G@@T TYPE@]@@@@ SERVO.     @#@@@@1PROCESSOR OUTPUT @#@@@@2I/O ATTEMPTS     QW
)@@G@@@E@@@@ THE RAT PROCESSOR WILL TRY TO READ THE TAPE BY DYNAMICALLY @E@@@@QX
)@@G@@ CHANGING THE PARITY AND DENSITY MODES (IF THE 'N' OPTION   @E@@@@ IS NOQY
)@@G@@T SPECIFIED) AND USING SUPPRESS RECOVERY MODE. FOR    @D@@@@ EVERY READ QZ
)@@G@@ATTEMPT, THE DENSITY AND PARITY WILL BE   @#@@@@ PRINTED OUT.     @]@@@@RA
)@@G@@SPACE 1     @E@@@@ ALL I/O ATTEMPTS WILL BE DONE WITH TRANSLATIONS TURNERB
)@@G@@D     @E@@@@ OFF. FOR MSA DRIVES, THE MSA DATA TRANSFER FORMAT WILL     RC
)@@G@@@D@@@@ BE THE SAME AS THE ASSIGNMENT DEFAULTS, VIZ., FOR    @E@@@@ SEVENRD
)@@G@@ TRACK DRIVES, 6-BIT PACKED, FOR NINE TRACK DRIVES,   @#@@@@ 8-BIT PACKERE
)@@G@@D.    @]@@@@SPACE 1     @F@@@@ A MAXUMUM OF 2048 WORDS CAN BE READ FROM RF
)@@G@@THE TAPE. A WARNING     @C@@@@ WILL BE ISSUED IF THE BLOCK COULD BE BIGGRG
)@@G@@ER.   @]@@@@2I/O STATUS @E@@@@ FOR ALL READ ATTEMPTS THE I/O HARDWARE I/RH
)@@G@@O STATUS' RETURNED@E@@@@ BY THE EXEC WILL BE PRINTED. THIS WILL INCLUDE RI
)@@G@@THE CONTENTS@E@@@@ OF LOWER A1 FOR ALL READ ATTEMPTS AND THE MSA SENSE BRJ
)@@G@@YTES  @E@@@@ FOR U12/16/20 SERVOS. IF ABNORMAL FRAME COUNT, END OF FILE,RK
)@@G@@@E@@@@ OR END OF TAPE CONDITIONS OCCUR, THE USER WILL BE INFORMED.@]@@@@RL
)@@G@@SPACE 1     @E@@@@ IF A READ ATTEMPT FAILS AND DATA WAS PASSED ON THE TARM
)@@G@@PE,   @D@@@@ THE TAPE WILL BE MOVED BACK A BLOCK BEFORE THE RETRY.@D@@@@RN
)@@G@@ IF AN END OF FILE IS DETECTED, THE NEXT BLOCK WILL BE@[@@@@ READ.@[@@@@RO
)@@G@@2DUMPS@C@@@@ AS AN AID IN ANALYSING THE DATA ON THE TAPE,   @A@@@@ THE FRP
)@@G@@IRST 64 WORDS OF THE BLOCK    @E@@@@ WILL BE DUMPED IN VARIOUS FORMATS. RQ
)@@G@@CURRENTLY THESE INCLUDE @E@@@@ OCTAL, HEXADECIMAL, FIELDATA, ASCII, EBCDRR
)@@G@@IC, BCD AND XS-3. @E@@@@ AFTER THE INITIAL DUMPS THE DATA WILL BE ASSUMERS
)@@G@@D TO BE     @D@@@@ IN 8-BIT PACKED FORMAT. (ALTHOUGH THIS IS USUALLY    RT
)@@G@@@D@@@@ MEANINGFUL FOR NINE TRACK TAPES, ANY TAPE COULD BE   @D@@@@ IN THRU
)@@G@@IS FORMAT. FOR EXAMPLE, ANSI LABELS.) THE DATA  @B@@@@ WILL BE 'UNPACKEDRV
)@@G@@' AND DUMPED AGAIN.     @]@@@@SPACE 1     @E@@@@ IT IS ENTIRELY POSSIBLERW
)@@G@@ THAT THE CHARACTER DUMPS WOULD     @D@@@@ LOOK LIKE GARBAGE DUE TO AN IRX
)@@G@@NCORRECT MSA TRANSFER   @E@@@@ FORMAT BEING SELECTED. IF THIS APPEARS TORY
)@@G@@ BE THE CASE,     @E@@@@ THE @MODE COMMAND CAN BE USED TO CHANGE IT AND RZ
)@@G@@RAT CAN     @D@@@@ THEN BE RE-EXECUTED WITH THE 'N' OPTION FOR MORE     SA
)@@G@@@]@@@@ DUMPS.     @^@@@@1FUTURE ENHANCEMENTS    @E@@@@ IN THE FUTURE THESB
)@@G@@ PROCESSOR SHOULD BE GIVEN THE CAPABILITY @E@@@@ OF DUMPING A REQUESTED SC
)@@G@@NUMBER OF BLOCKS. IT SHOULD ALSO    @F@@@@ ALLOW THE USER TO SELECT THE SD
)@@G@@CHARACTER DUMPS THAT HE DESIRES.    @ @@@@ AND, IT SHOULD BE REUSABLE.  SE
)@@G@@___^+)HIS IS USUALLY    ======@@^@@ @@@@@@@@@@@@@@ @T"@@@@@]@@@@@@@@@@@@SF

)@@G@@IS CODE IS ENTERED WHEN THE REEL NUMBER TYPED IN BY THE     @G@@@B.     WJ
)@@G@@    OPERATOR DISAGREES WITH THE REEL NUMBER RETURNED VIA TSWAP$.  @G@@@BWK

)@@G@@GAIN. @G@@@B.         IF THE TAPE IS IMPROPERLY LABELED, THE OPERATOR SHWQ

)@@G@@.                             P     @[@@@@.     @[@@@@.     @F@@@@. SCRIGF
)@@G@@PT IS A REWRITE OF A PROGRAM WHICH ONCE EXISTED AT CHI.     @F@@@@. THOSGG
)@@G@@E ALREADY FAMILIAR WITH THE CHI VERSION MAY  SKIP  THIS     @F@@@@. DESCGH
)@@G@@RIPTION;  HOWEVER, THEY WILL PROBABLY RUN INTO PROBLEMS     @F@@@@. SINCGI
)@@G@@E THE USE,  CALLING  SEQUENCE,  INPUT  AND  OUTPUT  ARE     @]@@@@. DIFFGJ
)@@G@@ERENT.@[@@@@.     @B@@@@. A TYPICAL SCRIPT CALL WOULD LOOK LIKE:  @[@@@@GK
)@@G@@.     @ @@@@.         @SCRIPT,F LOUISE    @A@@@@.         $HAPPY $BIRTHDGL
)@@G@@AY $LOUISE! @[@@@@.     @F@@@@. WHILE  SOMEWHAT  TRITE,  THIS  WOULD  HAGM
)@@G@@VE  THE  (GENERALLY     @F@@@@. DESIRABLE)  EFFECT  OF  PRODUCING THE WOGN
)@@G@@RDS 'HAPPY BIRTHDAY     @F@@@@. LOUISE!' IN ENORMOUS SCRIPT LETTERS  ALOGO
)@@G@@NG  THE  LENGTH  OF     @F@@@@. ABOUT  FIVE  PAGES.  THE FIRST LETTER OFGP
)@@G@@ EACH WORD WOULD BE     @F@@@@. IN UPPER CASE AS THEY HAVE BEEN PRECEEDEGQ
)@@G@@D  BY  THE  FORCING     @F@@@@. CHARACTER  ('$')  AND  THE  'F' OPTION WGR
)@@G@@AS SPECIFIED ON THE     @F@@@@. PROCESSOR CALL.  THE LARGE LETTERS WOULDGS
)@@G@@ BE COMPOSED OF THE     @F@@@@. LETTERS  'L',  'O',  'U',  'I',  'S',  AGT
)@@G@@ND  'E' REPEATED AS     @F@@@@. NECESSARY.  (IF LOUISE HAD NOT  BEEN  PLGU
)@@G@@ACED  ON  THE  CALL     @F@@@@. CARD,  THE  DEFAULT  CHARACTER,  '%',  WGV
)@@G@@OULD HAVE BEEN USED     @]@@@@. INSTEAD.) @[@@@@.     @F@@@@. THE USE OFGW
)@@G@@ THE 'F' OPTION SHOULD  BE  RESTRICTED  TO  THOSE     @F@@@@. CALLS  WHIGX
)@@G@@CH  CANNOT  PROVIDE UPPER/LOWER CASE MESSAGES VIA     @F@@@@. THE INPUT GY
)@@G@@MEDIUM.  WITHOUT THE 'F' OPTION, THE OUTPUT  WILL     @C@@@@. APPEAR EXAGZ
)@@G@@CTLY AS THE INPUT (ONLY BIGGER).    @[@@@@.     @F@@@@. THE  OTHER  OPTIHA
)@@G@@ONS  RELEVANT TO SCRIPT ARE THE 'D' AND 'B'     @F@@@@. OPTIONS WHICH REHB
)@@G@@SULT CORRESPONDINGLY IN 'DEMAND' FORMAT AND     @E@@@@. 'BATCH' FORMAT RHC
)@@G@@EGARDLESS OF THE ACTUAL MODE OF THE RUN.  @[@@@@.     @[@@@@.     @[@@@@HD

)@@G@@          TNE,U     A9,FORCE            YES -- IS THIS THE FORCING CHARAKM

)@@G@@CHAR            NO -- LEAVE IT ALONE@G@@@@          A,U       A9,040    KR

)@@G@@    IS IT A SPACE?@F@@@@ISSPACE   A,U       A13,SPACE           LEAVE 'SKV

)@@G@@1)    @F@@@@          TLE       A12,X9              SEGMENT ON CURRENT LLU
)@@G@@INE?  @H@@@@          LMJ       A1,PRINT            NO -- CLOSE OUT THE LV
)@@G@@PREVIOUS LINE     @G@@@@          LUF       A2,A12              SET UP TLW
)@@G@@O COMPUTE STORE INDEX   @F@@@@          TOP       A5,OPT(OPTION('D')) DELX

)@@G@@*[S@@@*SDFF*@#@@@@SCRIPT PROCESSOR  @]@@@[OPTION P,ON @]@[@@1DESCRIPTIONDK
)@@G@@@]@@@[SPACE 3     @E@@@@ SCRIPT IS A REWRITE OF A PROGRAM WHICH ONCE EXIDL
)@@G@@STED AT CHI.@E@@@@ THOSE ALREADY FAMILIAR WITH THE CHI VERSION MAY  SKIPDM
)@@G@@  THIS@E@@@@ DESCRIPTION;  HOWEVER, THEY WILL PROBABLY RUN INTO PROBLEMSDN
)@@G@@@E@@@@ SINCE THE USE,  CALLING  SEQUENCE,  INPUT  AND  OUTPUT  ARE@]@@@@DO
)@@G@@ DIFFERENT. @@@@@@@B@@@@ A TYPICAL SCRIPT CALL WOULD LOOK LIKE:   @@@@@@DP
)@@G@@@ @@@@         @SCRIPT,F LOUISE     @A@@@@         $HAPPY $BIRTHDAY $LOUDQ
)@@G@@ISE!  @@@@@@@E@@@@ WHILE  SOMEWHAT  TRITE,  THIS  WOULD  HAVE  THE  (GENDR
)@@G@@ERALLY@E@@@@ DESIRABLE)  EFFECT  OF  PRODUCING THE WORDS 'HAPPY BIRTHDAYDS
)@@G@@@E@@@@ LOUISE!' IN ENORMOUS SCRIPT LETTERS  ALONG  THE  LENGTH  OF@E@@@@DT
)@@G@@ ABOUT  FIVE  PAGES.  THE FIRST LETTER OF EACH WORD WOULD BE@E@@@@ IN UPDU
)@@G@@PER CASE AS THEY HAVE BEEN PRECEEDED  BY  THE  FORCING@E@@@@ CHARACTER  DV
)@@G@@('$')  AND  THE  'F' OPTION WAS SPECIFIED ON THE@E@@@@ PROCESSOR CALL.  DW
)@@G@@THE LARGE LETTERS WOULD BE COMPOSED OF THE@E@@@@ LETTERS  'L',  'O',  'UDX
)@@G@@',  'I',  'S',  AND  'E' REPEATED AS@E@@@@ NECESSARY.  (IF LOUISE HAD NODY
)@@G@@T  BEEN  PLACED  ON  THE  CALL@E@@@@ CARD,  THE  DEFAULT  CHARACTER,  '%DZ
)@@G@@',  WOULD HAVE BEEN USED@]@@@@ INSTEAD.)  @@@@@@@E@@@@ THE USE OF THE 'FEA
)@@G@@' OPTION SHOULD  BE  RESTRICTED  TO  THOSE@E@@@@ CALLS  WHICH  CANNOT  PEB
)@@G@@ROVIDE UPPER/LOWER CASE MESSAGES VIA@E@@@@ THE INPUT MEDIUM.  WITHOUT THEC
)@@G@@E 'F' OPTION, THE OUTPUT  WILL@C@@@@ APPEAR EXACTLY AS THE INPUT (ONLY BED
)@@G@@IGGER).     @@@@@@@E@@@@ THE  OTHER  OPTIONS  RELEVANT TO SCRIPT ARE THEEE
)@@G@@ 'D' AND 'B'@E@@@@ OPTIONS WHICH RESULT CORRESPONDINGLY IN 'DEMAND' FORMEF
)@@G@@AT AND@E@@@@ 'BATCH' FORMAT REGARDLESS OF THE ACTUAL MODE OF THE RUN.   EG
